"a pet store had 2 dogs . on sunday they got 5 more . on monday they got 3 more . how many dogs does the pet store have now ?" ; "The pet store initially had 2 dogs. On Sunday, they got 5 more dogs, and on Monday, they got 3 more dogs. To find out how many dogs the pet store has now, we can add the number of dogs they had initially to the number of dogs they acquired on Sunday and Monday.

Number of dogs initially = 2
Number of dogs acquired on Sunday = 5
Number of dogs acquired on Monday = 3

To find the total number of dogs, we can add these three numbers together:

Total number of dogs = Number of dogs initially + Number of dogs acquired on Sunday + Number of dogs acquired on Monday

Total number of dogs = 2 + 5 + 3

Calculating this expression gives us:

Total number of dogs = 10

Therefore, the pet store now has 10 dogs.

#### 10"

"a pet shelter had 23 puppies when another 2 were brought in . if 5 puppies a day are adopted how long would it take for all of them to be adopted ?" ; "To solve this problem, we need to determine how many puppies are left after each day and calculate the number of days it takes for all of them to be adopted.

Initially, the pet shelter had 23 puppies. When another 2 puppies were brought in, the total number of puppies became 23 + 2 = 25.

Each day,5 puppies are adopted. So, after the first day, there will be 25 - 5 = 20 puppies left.

After the second day, there will be 20 - 5 = 15 puppies left.

We can continue this pattern until there are no more puppies left.

After the third day, there will be 15 - 5 = 10 puppies left.
After the fourth day, there will be 10 - 5 = 5 puppies left.
After the fifth day, there will be 5 - 5 = 0 puppies left.

Therefore, it would take a total of 5 days for all of the puppies to be adopted.

"zoe was unboxing some of her old winter clothes . she found 8 boxes of clothing and inside each box there were 4 scarves and 6 mittens . how many pieces of winter clothing did zoe have total ?" ; "To find the total number of winter clothing pieces Zoe has, we need to multiply the number of boxes by the sum of scarves and mittens in each box.

Number of boxes = 8
Number of scarves in each box = 4
Number of mittens in each box = 6

Total number of winter clothing pieces = Number of boxes * (Number of scarves + Number of mittens)

Total number of winter clothing pieces = 8 * (4 + 6)

Calculating the sum inside the parentheses:
4 + 6 = 10

Substituting the values back into the equation:
Total number of winter clothing pieces = 8 * 10

Calculating the multiplication:
8 * 10 = 80

Therefore, Zoe has a total of 80 pieces of winter clothing.

To find their combined rate, we add their individual rates: Bob's rate + Tim's rate = 50 feet per hour + 37.5 feet per hour = 87.5 feet per hour.

Therefore, Bob and Tim working together can make 350 feet of rope in 4 hours.

"There were 28 bales of hay in the barn . Tim stacked bales in the barn today . There are now 54 bales of hay in the barn . How many bales did he store in the barn ?" ; "Let's assume that Tim stacked x bales of hay in the barn today.

Initially, there were 28 bales of hay in the barn. After Tim stacked x bales, the total number of bales became 28 + x.

According to the problem, there are now 54 bales of hay in the barn. So we can set up the equation:

28 + x = 54

To find the value of x, we need to isolate it on one side of the equation. We can do this by subtracting 28 from both sides:

x = 54 - 28

Now we can calculate the value of x:

x = 26

Therefore, Tim stored 26 bales of hay in the barn.

"The cafeteria had 62 apples . For lunch they handed out 8 to students and decided to use the rest to make pies . If each pie takes 9 apples , how many pies could they make ?" ; "To solve this problem, we can use the following steps:

1. Start with the total number of apples in the cafeteria, which is 62.

2. Next, subtract the number of apples handed out to students, which is 8. This will give us the number of apples remaining to make pies.

3. Now, we need to divide the remaining number of apples by the number of apples needed to make one pie, which is 9.

4. Finally, we will have the number of pies that can be made.

Let's calculate it step by step:

Step 1: Total number of apples = 62.
Step 2: Remaining apples = Total number of apples - Apples handed out to students = 62 - 8 = 54.
Step 3: Number of pies = Remaining apples / Apples per pie = 54 / 9 = 6.

Therefore, they can make 6 pies.

If Emily scored 23 points and everyone else scored 2 points each, the total number of points scored by everyone else can be calculated as (x - 1) * 2.

The total number of points scored by the team is the sum of Emily's points and the points scored by everyone else, which is equal to 39.

So, we can write the equation:

23 + (x - 1) * 2 = 39

Simplifying this equation:

23 + 2x - 2 = 39

Combining like terms:

2x + 21 = 39

Subtracting 21 from both sides:

2x = 18

Dividing both sides by 2:

x = 9

Therefore, there were 9 players on Emily's team.

"Hayley had 25 meatballs on her plate . Kirsten stole some of her meatballs . Now she has 11 meatballs on her plate . How many meatballs did Kirsten steal ?" ; "Let's assume that Kirsten stole x meatballs from Hayley's plate. 

Initially, Hayley had 25 meatballs on her plate. If Kirsten stole x meatballs, then the number of meatballs left on Hayley's plate would be 25 - x.

According to the problem, Hayley now has 11 meatballs on her plate. So we can set up the equation:

25 - x = 11

To find the value of x, we need to isolate it on one side of the equation. We can do this by subtracting 25 from both sides:

25 - x - 25 = 11 - 25
-x = -14

To solve for x, we multiply both sides of the equation by -1:

(-1)(-x) = (-1)(-14)
x = 14

Therefore, Kirsten stole 14 meatballs from Hayley's plate.

>>2 = 46x

<<2 / 46 = x

>>1/23 = x

"a chef had 46 apples . after making some pies he had 14 left . how many apples did he use ?" ; "Let's denote the number of apples the chef used as ""x"". 

The chef started with 46 apples and after making some pies, he had 14 left. This can be represented as an equation: 

46 - x = 14

To find the value of ""x"", we need to isolate it on one side of the equation. We can do this by subtracting 14 from both sides:

46 - 14 - x = 14 - 14
32 - x = 0

Now, to solve for ""x"", we need to isolate it completely. We can do this by subtracting 32 from both sides:

32 - x - 32 = 0 - 32
-x = -32

To get the value of ""x"" alone, we multiply both sides by -1 (since multiplying or dividing both sides of an equation by a negative number reverses the inequality):

(-1)(-x) = (-1)(-32)
x = 32

Therefore, the chef used 32 apples.

"my car gets 20 miles per gallon . how many miles can i drive on 5 gallons of gas ?" ; "To solve this problem, we need to understand the relationship between miles per gallon (mpg) and gallons of gas. The question states that the car gets 20 miles per gallon. This means that for every gallon of gas, the car can travel 20 miles.

Now, the question asks how many miles can be driven on 5 gallons of gas. To find this, we need to multiply the number of gallons by the miles per gallon. This is based on the principle of direct proportion, where the product of the two quantities remains constant. In this case, the two quantities are the number of gallons and the miles that can be driven on those gallons.

So, the calculation would be:

 5 * 20 = << 5 * 20 = 100 >> 100 

This means that you can drive 100 miles on 5 gallons of gas.

"dave had 16 apps on his phone . after deleting some he had 8 left . how many apps did he delete ?" ; "Let's assume that Dave deleted x number of apps from his phone. 

Initially, Dave had 16 apps on his phone, and after deleting some, he had 8 left. 

So, we can set up the equation: 

16 - x = 8

To find the value of x, we need to isolate it on one side of the equation. 

Subtracting 16 from both sides of the equation:

16 - x - 16 = 8 - 16

Simplifying:

-x = -8

To solve for x, we can multiply both sides of the equation by -1 to get rid of the negative sign:

(-1)(-x) = (-1)(-8)

Simplifying:

x = 8

Therefore, Dave deleted 8 apps from his phone.

18 - x - 9 = 9 - 9
9 - x = 0

Since any number subtracted from itself equals zero, we can simplify further: 
-x = 0

To isolate ""x"" and solve for it, we multiply both sides of the equation by -1 (to change the sign): 
(-1)(-x) = (-1)(0)
x = 0

Therefore, no cookies were eaten.

"On a recent trip to CA , we averaged 50 miles per hour . On the return trip we averaged 60 miles per hour . Determine the average speed of the trip to CA and back ." ; "To determine the average speed of the trip to CA and back, we can use the concept of harmonic mean. The harmonic mean is calculated by dividing the total distance traveled by the total time taken.

Let's assume that the distance to CA is D miles. Therefore, the distance back from CA is also D miles.

The time taken to travel to CA at an average speed of 50 miles per hour can be calculated using the formula: time = distance / speed. So, the time taken to travel to CA is D / 50 hours.

Similarly, the time taken to travel back from CA at an average speed of 60 miles per hour is D / 60 hours.

The total distance traveled for the round trip is 2D miles (D miles to CA + D miles back from CA).

The total time taken for the round trip is (D / 50) + (D / 60) hours.

Now, we can calculate the average speed using the formula: average speed = total distance / total time.

Substituting in the values we have:

average speed = (2D) / ((D / 50) + (D / 60))

To simplify this expression, we need to find a common denominator for (D / 50) and (D / 60). The least common multiple of 50 and 60 is 300.

average speed = (2D) / ((6D/300) + (5D/300))

Combining like terms:

average speed = (2D) / ((11D/300))

Dividing both numerator and denominator by D:

average speed = (2/11) * (300)

Calculating this expression:

average speed = 600/11

"The distance measured on a map varies directly with the actual distance . If 1 cm represents 25 kilometers , how many kilometers are represented by 7 cm ?" ; "To solve this problem, we can set up a proportion using the given information.

Let's assume that x represents the number of kilometers represented by 7 cm on the map.

According to the given information, 1 cm represents 25 kilometers. Therefore, we can set up the following proportion:

1 / t cm}25 t{ km} = <<1 / t cm}25 t{ km} = 7 / t cm}x t{ km}>> 7 / t cm}x t{ km}

Initial number of orange balloons: 9
Number of lost orange balloons: 2

To find the number of orange balloons Sally has now, we subtract the number of lost orange balloons from the initial number of orange balloons:

9 - 2 = <<9 - 2 = 7>> 7

Therefore, Sally has 7 orange balloons now.

The total number of chips in the bowl is given by adding the number of red, blue, and green chips together:

4 + 3 + 9 = <<4 + 3 + 9 = 16>> 16

Now, let's calculate the number of non-red chips. Since we want to exclude the red chips, we only need to consider the blue and green chips:

3 + 9 = <<3 + 9 = 12>> 12

Therefore, there are 12 non-red chips out of a total of 16 chips.

To find the probability, we divide the number of non-red chips by the total number of chips:

1 / 216 = <<1 / 216 = 3 / 4>> 3 / 4

- Each box holds 6 blocks.
- There are 5 boxes in a case.

Next, we need to consider the number of boxes in a case. Since there are 5 boxes in a case and we have already calculated that George has 2 boxes, we can add these quantities together to find the total number of boxes that George has. This gives us 2 + 5 = <<2 + 5 = 7>> 7 boxes.

Finally, we can multiply the total number of blocks in each box by the total number of boxes to find the total number of blocks that George has. This gives us 12 * 7 = <<12 * 7 = 84>> 84 blocks.

"Sarah had 55 homework problems . She finished 6 of them but still had 7 pages of problems to do . If each page has the same number of problems on it , how many problems are on each page ?" ; "Sarah had 55 homework problems. She finished 6 of them but still had 7 pages of problems to do. Let's assume that each page has the same number of problems on it, and we'll call this unknown number of problems ""x"".

The total number of problems Sarah finished is 6, and she still has 7 pages of problems to do. Since each page has the same number of problems, the total number of problems on those 7 pages is 7 times x.

So, we can set up an equation: 

6 + 7x = 55

To solve for x, we need to isolate it on one side of the equation. We can start by subtracting 6 from both sides:

7x = 55 - 6

Simplifying the right side:

7x = 49

Now, to solve for x, we divide both sides by 7:

x = 49 / 7

Simplifying the right side:

x = 7

Therefore, there are 7 problems on each page.

On Tuesday, Dave worked 2 hours and made 6 dollars per hour. So his earnings on Tuesday can be calculated as:

"In Shannon 's apartment complex , 0.16666666666666666 the apartments are one - bedroom apartments and 0.3333333333333333 are two - bedroom apartments . What fraction of the apartments are either 1 - or two - bedroom apartments ?" ; "To find the fraction of apartments that are either one-bedroom or two-bedroom, we need to add the fractions of one-bedroom and two-bedroom apartments together.

The fraction of one-bedroom apartments is 0.16666666666666666, and the fraction of two-bedroom apartments is 0.3333333333333333.

To add these fractions, we need to find a common denominator. The smallest number that both 6 and 3 divide into evenly is 6.

Converting the fractions to have a denominator of 6:
- The fraction of one-bedroom apartments becomes 1/6 (since 1 multiplied by 6 equals 6).
- The fraction of two-bedroom apartments becomes 2/6 (since 2 multiplied by 3 equals 6).

Now we can add these fractions together:
1/6 + 2/6 = (1 + 2)/6 = 3/6

Simplifying the fraction, we can divide both the numerator and denominator by their greatest common divisor, which is 3:
3/6 = (3 / 3)/(6 / 3) = 1/2

Therefore, the fraction of apartments that are either one-bedroom or two-bedroom is 1/2.
